     <h1 dir="ltr">
      Supercharge Your Morning CoffeeWith Butter?
     </h1>
     <p dir="ltr">
      Coffee shouldnt be a short-term caffeine boost followed by a headache and a crash. It can jump-start your body with the right fats, right when your body is craving them.
     </p>
     <p>
      Bulletproof Coffee is made with Upgraded Coffee Beans, grass-fed butter, and Brain Octane Oil blended to give you an unfair advantage after your morning routine.
     </p>
     <p dir="ltr">
      This exact recipe works every day, not just for me, but for chart-topping musicians, professional poker players, MMA fights, olympic athletes, entrepreneurs, and Fortune 500 CEOs.
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>
     <center>
      <iframe allowfullscreen="allowfullscreen" frameborder="0" height="315" src="//www.youtube.com/embed/4YjLMdx3YZY" width="560">
      </iframe>
     </center>

    <section>
     <h2>
      Great Coffee Articles
     </h2>
     <div class="row">
      <article class="col-xs-12 col-sm-4 col-lg-4">
       <img src="//www.bulletproofexec.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/03/Coffee-Cherries-e1436294410691.jpg"/>
       <p>
        <a href="/why-bad-coffee-makes-you-weak/">
         Why Bad Coffee Makes You Weak
        </a>
       </p>
      </article>
      <article class="col-xs-12 col-sm-4 col-lg-4">
       <img src="//www.bulletproofexec.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/04/iStock_000007412783_ExtraSmall-150x150.jpg"/>
       <p>
        <a href="/mastering-the-mid-day-recharge-in-only-15-minutes/">
         Mastering the Mid-day Recharge (In 15 Minutes)
        </a>
       </p>
      </article>
      <article class="col-xs-12 col-sm-4 col-lg-4">
       <img src="//www.bulletproofexec.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/04/iStock_000009336597_ExtraSmall-150x150.jpg"/>
       <p>

         The 4 Secrets of Getting Wired on Caffeine
        </a>
       </p>
      </article>
     </div>
    </section>
   </div>

Simple tricks like upgrading your cup of coffee, sleeping smarter, all the way to consciously controlling your brainwaves, are possible with the right information. You can think faster, have limitless focus, laugh at food cravings, and
        </p>

    <div class="container category" id="page">
     <div class="row">
      <section class="detail col-xs-12 col-sm-12 col-md-8" id="leftcolumn">
       <article class="post-510 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-biohacking-2 category-bulletproofbody category-bulletproofdiet category-supplements category-detoxingbulletproof tag-breakfast tag-bulletproof-diet tag-diet tag-fat-burning tag-food tag-nutrition tag-performance tag-supplements" id="post-510">
        <header class="entry-header">
         <h1 class="entry-title">
          Upgrade Your Energy, Optimize Your Supplements
         </h1>
        </header>
        <div class="entry-content">
         <span class="blgimg">
         </span>
         <div class="ssba">
          <div style="text-align:left">
           Share:
           <a class="ssba_twitter_share" href="http://twitter.com/share?url=https://www.bulletproofexec.com/optimize-your-supplements/&amp;text=Upgrade+Your+Energy%2C+Optimize+Your+Supplements+" target="_blank">
            <img alt="Tweet about this on Twitter" class="ssba" src="//www.bulletproofexec.com/wp-content/plugins/simple-share-buttons-adder/buttons/simple/twitter.png" title="Twitter"/>
           </a>
           <a class="ssba_facebook_share" href="http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=https://www.bulletproofexec.com/optimize-your-supplements/" target="_blank">
            <img alt="Share on Facebook" class="ssba" src="//www.bulletproofexec.com/wp-content/plugins/simple-share-buttons-adder/buttons/simple/facebook.png" title="Facebook"/>
           </a>
           <a class="ssba_pinterest_share" href="javascript:void((function()%7Bvar%20e=document.createElement('script');e.setAttribute('type','text/javascript');e.setAttribute('charset','UTF-8');e.setAttribute('src','//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinmarklet.js?r='+Math.random()*99999999);document.body.appendChild(e)%7D)());">
            <img alt="Pin on Pinterest" class="ssba" src="//www.bulletproofexec.com/wp-content/plugins/simple-share-buttons-adder/buttons/simple/pinterest.png" title="Pinterest"/>
           </a>
           <a class="ssba_google_share" href="https://plus.google.com/share?url=https://www.bulletproofexec.com/optimize-your-supplements/" target="_blank">
            <img alt="Share on Google+" class="ssba" src="//www.bulletproofexec.com/wp-content/plugins/simple-share-buttons-adder/buttons/simple/google.png" title="Google+"/>
           </a>
           <a class="ssba_linkedin_share ssba_share_link" href="http://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;url=https://www.bulletproofexec.com/optimize-your-supplements/" target="_blank">
            <img alt="Share on LinkedIn" class="ssba" src="//www.bulletproofexec.com/wp-content/plugins/simple-share-buttons-adder/buttons/simple/linkedin.png" title="Linkedin"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <p>
          <img alt="" class="alignright" height="259" src="//ocw.jhsph.edu/courses/criticalanalysispopulardietssupplements/homePageImage.jpg" width="361"/>
         </p>
         <p>
          There are three groups of people when it comes to supplements.
         </p>
         <p>
          The first group are those who shun all forms of supplementation because
          <em>
           it isnt natural
          </em>
          or because
          <em>
           cavemen didnt have supplements.
          </em>
          They often say,
          <em>
           I dont need supplements because I get all my nutrients from food.
           <br/>
          </em>
          My somewhat obvious reply to that misguided belief is,
          <em>
           Then you must get all your toxins from nature.
          </em>
         </p>
         <p>
          The second group are those who think supplements can make up for a poor diet, high stress levels, and pretty much everything else.
         </p>
         <p>
          The final group is somewhere in between. This is where we want to be.
         </p>
         <p>
          Supplements are a double edged sword. The wrong ones can do more damage than good, but the right ones can massively improve your health, even if you eat a great diet. In this article, youre going to get an overview of the problems with generic supplements, how to pick the right supplements, and the list of supplements almost everyone should be taking.
         </p>
         <h2>
          Throw Away Your Multivitamins
         </h2>
         <p>
          With
          <a href="http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2011/04/13/vitamin-use_n_848777.html" target="_blank">
           half of the U.S. population taking a multivitamin
          </a>
          , many people seem to think multivitamins are the first line of defense against malnutrition and disease. In fact, the opposite is true. Multivitamins can actually do more harm than good. We wont go into the full details here, but here are two reasons to choose targeted supplements over multivitamins.
         </p>
         <h3>
          1. Imbalance of nutrients.
         </h3>
         <p>
          Most multivitamins have too much of some nutrients (like vitamin A or B6) and not enough of others (like magnesium). The result is over dosing and under dosing at the same time. In order to get enough of some vitamins and minerals, you would have to take far more than you should of others. It is a common practice to use very small amounts of expensive nutrients, which allows manufacturers to still list them on the label. Average consumers dont notice there are meaningless amounts of some nutrients, and they only want to take one pill anyway. There is no way to fit a complete spectrum of nutrients in one single pill.
         </p>
         <h3>
          2. Low quality.
         </h3>
         <p>
          Nutrients come in different forms that behave differently inside your body. Folate is an essential B vitamin, but folic acid, the kind found in generic multivitamins,
          <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/19190501" target="_blank">
           increases your risk of cancer
          </a>
          . This may be why
          <a href="http://well.blogs.nytimes.com/2009/02/09/study-finds-no-benefit-from-daily-multivitamin/" target="_blank">
           many studies show no benefit to taking multivitamins
          </a>
          (although honestly, thats more likely because pharmaceutical companies funded those studies) In fact,
          <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/21987192" target="_blank">
           much of the research shows an increased risk of mortality
          </a>
          . This is assuming you even absorb the ingredients. Many multivitamins are made with fillers and additives which are poorly utilized by the body  to the extent some nursing homes call them bedpan bullets. Even if they have the right amount of a nutrient on the label, very little may reach your cells.
         </p>
         <p>
          In the end, you get what you pay for with supplements. You can delude yourself and buy the generic multivitamins at Costco, or you can spend a little extra and actually do something to improve your health.
         </p>
         <p>
          Before we get into the exact supplements you should take, here are some general criteria for supplementation.
         </p>
         <ol>
          <li>
           Get the majority of your nutrients from food.
          </li>
          <li>
           Consume supplements in their highest performance form.
          </li>
          <li>
           When in doubt  go without.
          </li>
          <li>
           Recognize that some supplements can help your performance  and health  more than food.
          </li>
         </ol>
         <h3>
          Get the majority of your nutrients from food.
         </h3>
         <p>
          You dont eat nutrients  you eat food. Whole foods behave differently from their individual parts. The nutrients from a piece of meat are more bioavailable than consuming the equivalent nutrients from a pill. Studies have shown that
          <a href="http://cdn.marksdailyapple.com/wordpress/wp-content/uploads/2010/12/McAfeeGrassfedbeefbettern3thanconventionalbeefBJN2011-2.pdf" target="_blank">
           grass-fed meat boosts plasma omega-3 levels far more than what could be explained by the actual omega-3 content of the meat
          </a>
          . Antioxidants from food are usually beneficial, but taking mega-doses of some synthetic antioxidants increases your risk of death. The nutrients in food work together in a process known as
          <a href="http://www.ajcn.org/content/89/5/1543S.abstract" target="_blank">
           food synergy
          </a>
          . In short, this means food is more powerful than the sum of its parts. The good news is the
          <a href="https://www.upgradedself.com/bulletproof-diet-roadmap-poster?utm_source=post&amp;utm_medium=blog&amp;utm_campaign=bulletproof-upgraded-coffee" target="_blank">
           Bulletproof Diet
          </a>
          is the most nutrient packed diet in the world. If you havent yet, take the time to read the
          <a href="http://www.bulletproofexec.com/top-8-personal-upgrades-series-introduction/" target="_blank" title="Top 8 Personal Upgrades: Series Introduction">
           first article in this series
          </a>
          to learn more about the
          <a href="https://www.upgradedself.com/bulletproof-diet-roadmap-poster?utm_source=post&amp;utm_medium=blog&amp;utm_campaign=bulletproof-upgraded-coffee" target="_blank">
           Bulletproof Diet
          </a>
          .
         </p>
         <h3>
          Consume supplements in their highest performance form.
         </h3>
         <p>
          Artificial forms of nutrients are not as effective as the real thing. When you do supplement, you should still try to get them from whole food sources. Isolated nutrients often compete for the same absorption pathways. For example, iron and calcium inhibit the absorption of one another, but synthetic nutrients are often damaging. For these reasons, nutrients should be consumed in their most natural form possible.
         </p>
         <h3>
          When in doubt  go without.
         </h3>
         <p>
          There is always a risk with supplements. Even the most natural forms can contain high levels of heavy metals, contaminants, and byproducts from processing. Food is not guaranteed to be free from these substances, but its far less likely to contain them. In many cases, the biggest downside to taking supplements you dont need is simply expensive urine, but in other cases its better to go without than to take something you shouldnt have.
         </p>
         <h2>
          What SupplementsYou Should Take
         </h2>
         <p>
          I take over 40 pills a day, carefully selected for my own needs using testing over the last decade. Thats why this isnt called the complete guide to supplementation. This list does not cover my recommendations for smart drugs or most brain enhancing nutrients. Those topics will come in a later post. These are the basic supplements that most everyone should be taking.
         </p>
         <p>
          For each nutrient, you will get a:
         </p>
         <ul>
          <li>
           Dosage recommendation.
          </li>
          <li>
           The correct form it should be taken in.
          </li>
          <li>
           The time it should be taken.
          </li>
          <li>
           A recommended brand.
          </li>
         </ul>
         <p>
          I have no relation or affiliation with any of these companies. They are simply the ones I trust with my health and use on a daily basis.
         </p>
         <p>
          Here are the ten nutrients (almost) everyone should supplement with.
         </p>
         <ol>
          <li>
           Vitamin D
          </li>
          <li>
           Magnesium
          </li>
          <li>
           Vitamin K2
          </li>
          <li>
           Vitamin C
          </li>
          <li>
           Iodine
          </li>
          <li>
           Krill Oil
          </li>
          <li>
           Vitamin A
          </li>
          <li>
           Selenium
          </li>
          <li>
           Copper
          </li>
          <li>
           Folinic Acid with B12
          </li>
         </ol>
         <h2>
          Vitamin D
         </h2>
         <p>
          Vitamin D isnt just the most important supplement  it is possibly
          <a href="http://www.bulletproofexec.com/top-6-biohacks/" target="_blank">
           the most important biohack
          </a>
          . Vitamin D acts on over 1000 different genes and serves as a substrate for sex hormones like testosterone, human growth hormone, and estrogen. It moderates immune function and inflammation. It assists in calcium metabolism and bone formation. Its no coincidence this is one of the few vitamins humans can make on their own. Without it  wed be dead. Its true that you can get adequate vitamin D from sun exposure, but for non-nudist non-equatorial dwellers its not enough. If youre getting adequate vitamin A, its almost impossible to overdose on D.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Dose:
          </strong>
          1000 IU / 25 pounds of body weight.*
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Form:
          </strong>
          D3
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Time Taken:
          </strong>
          Morning
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Recommended Brand:
          </strong>
          Purity Products vitamin D3
         </p>
         <p>
          *People with brown/black skin dont convert sunlight into vitamin D as quickly as lighter skinned people. If youre brown skinned, a safe bet is 1500 IU / 25 pounds of body weight, but you should always test your blood levels because individual response to dosage varies.
         </p>
         <h2>
          Magnesium
         </h2>
         <p>
          This is almost as important as vitamin D, and almost as under appreciated. Magnesium is used in over 300 enzymatic processes, including all of those involved in ATP production. Its also vital for proper transcription of DNA and RNA.
         </p>
         <p>
          Magnesium deficiency is a serious problem. Symptoms include heart arrhythmias, tachycardia, headaches, muscle cramps, nausea, metabolic syndrome, migraines, and pretty much everything else you dont want. Its also associated with cardiovascular disease diabetes, asthma, anxiety disorders, and PMS.
         </p>
         <p>
          Almost all Americans are deficient in magnesium. The
          <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/12949381?dopt=AbstractPlus" target="_blank">
           majority of people dont meet the RDA
          </a>
          , which is already too low. Due to soil depletion and poor farming practices, its almost impossible to get enough magnesium from your diet. Without a doubt  everyone should supplement with magnesium.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Dose:
          </strong>
          600-800mg / day
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Forms:
          </strong>
          Citrate, malate, glycinate, threonate, or orotate
          <strong>
           <br/>
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Time Taken:
          </strong>
          before bedtime.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Recommended Brand:
          </strong>
          Natural Calm or VRP
          <strong>
           <br/>
          </strong>
         </p>
         <h2>
          Vitamin K2
         </h2>
         <p>
          Unless you grew up eating only
          <a href="http://www.bulletproofexec.com/grass-fed-meat-part-1/" target="_blank">
           grass-fed meat
          </a>
          and raw milk  youre deficient in vitamin K2. Vitamin K2 is a fat soluble vitamin involved in calcium metabolism. Excess calcium is deposited in arteries, leading to calcification and decreased vascular function. This is why vitamin K2
          <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/18722618" target="_blank">
           prevents atherosclerosis and heart attacks
          </a>
          , and
          <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/16801507" target="_blank">
           strengthens bones
          </a>
          .
         </p>
         <p>
          Vitamin K1 is the kind of vitamin K found in leafy vegetables, and vitamin K2 is the kind found in grass-fed animal products. Humans dont convert vitamin K1 into K2 efficiently. Ruminant animals like cows and sheep convert K1 into K2 in their stomachs. This is
          <a href="http://www.bulletproofexec.com/grass-fed-meat-part-1/" target="_blank">
           another reason you should eat grass-fed animals
          </a>
          , because they can only get K1 from grass  not grains.
         </p>
         <p>
          There are two subsets of vitamin K2: MK-4, and MK-7. MK-4 is the kind shown to produce the most benefit, but MK-7 is still important. You should consume a total of at least 2,000mcg per day of K2, at least 100mcg of which should be the MK-7 form.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Dose:
          </strong>
          2,000mcg / day (100mcg MK-7 form)
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Forms:
          </strong>
          MK-4, and MK-7
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Time Taken:
          </strong>
          Doesnt really matter, but its best to take this with vitamin D, so morning is best.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Recommended Brand:
          </strong>
          Life Extension
         </p>
         <h2>
          Vitamin C
         </h2>
         <p>
          This is one of the safest, most effect supplements you can take. Vitamin C is needed for collagen and connective tissue formation. Its used to manufacture
          <a href="https://www.upgradedself.com/products/bulletproof-upgraded-glutathione-force?utm_source=post&amp;utm_medium=blog&amp;utm_campaign=bulletproof-upgraded-coffee" target="_blank" title="Upgraded Glutathione on Upgradedself.com">
           glutathione
          </a>
          , the most powerful antioxidant in the body. Vitamin C can enhance immune function and help quench free radical damage. Studies have shown you can take up to
          <a href="http://pmid.us/16570523" target="_blank">
           120 grams of vitamin C a day with no side effects
          </a>
          (besides loose stool).
         </p>
         <p>
          Its hard to get enough vitamin C from food, which is why
          <a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC1448351/" target="_blank">
           30 percent of the population is deficient
          </a>
          .
         </p>
         <p>
          Some fruits and vegetables are high in vitamin C, but cooking and storage methods can deplete vitamin C content. Supplementation with at least 500mg per day is optimal. You should take a lot more if you are suffering from chronic infections or healing from injury.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Dose:
          </strong>
          1-2 grams / day
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Forms:
          </strong>
          Ascorbic acid crystals or time release capsules.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Time Taken:
          </strong>
          Morning and evening, but its best not to take it after a workout as isolated antioxidants can negate the insulin sensitivity gained from exercise.
          <strong>
           <br/>
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Recommended Brand:
          </strong>
          Solaray
         </p>
         <h2>
          Iodine
         </h2>
         <p>
          Iodine is crucial for proper thyroid function and metabolism. It also enhances immune function and prevents brain damage. Iodine deficiency is widespread, so supplementation is wise. You can get some iodine from seafood, but risk of deficiency is still high. Iodized salt wont get you optimal levels. The toxic limit for iodine is also extremely high, meaning you can take a lot. A good starting point is 1mg / day from kelp powder or as potassium iodide.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Dose:
          </strong>
          1mg / day
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Forms:
          </strong>
          Kelp powder or potassium iodide capsules
          <strong>
           <br/>
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Time Taken:
          </strong>
          Doesnt matter.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Recommended Brand:
          </strong>
          Pure Encapsulations potassium iodide
          <strong>
           <br/>
          </strong>
         </p>
         <h2>
          EPA/DHA (Krill oil)
         </h2>
         <p>
          This is a tricky one. Small doses of high quality fish oil reduce inflammation, improve brain function, and even enhance muscle growth, but poor quality or high doses can cause more problems than they help to solve. Not all fish oil is created equal. Most of the brands you are likely to buy at your local grocery are contaminated, oxidized, and low potency. If you cant find a good fish oil  youre much better off avoiding it all together.
         </p>
         <p>
          Thats why I recommend krill oil over fish oil altogether. Krill is more stable and it is phosphorylated, meaning its easier for your brain to use. It also comes with astaxanthin, a potent antioxidant.
         </p>
         <p>
          There are real benefits to taking EPA and DHA, but most of these are strongest if your diet is deficient in omega-3s, or too high in omega-6s. If youre eating a Bulletproof Diet, this wont be a problem. Humans only need 350mg of DHA and EPA a day to have optimal brain function. If youre eating grass-fed meat and wild caught fish, this is easily obtainable. If you cant find grass-fed meat or wild caught seafood, you should supplement with at least 1000mg of krill oil per day.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Dose:
          </strong>
          1000mg / day
          <strong>
           <br/>
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Forms:
          </strong>
          Krill Oil
          <strong>
           <br/>
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Time Taken:
          </strong>
          With meals.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Recommended Brand:
          </strong>
          Jarrow
          <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B0013OULGA/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=390957&amp;creativeASIN=B0013OULGA&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=bulletpexecut-20">
           Krill oil
          </a>
          <img alt="" border="0" class="fxcolwyioezriznxzlja" height="1" src="//www.assoc-amazon.com/e/ir?t=bulletpexecut-20&amp;l=as2&amp;o=1&amp;a=B0013OULGA" style="border: none !important; margin: 0px !important;" width="1"/>
          <strong>
           <br/>
          </strong>
         </p>
         <p>
          In addition to these basic supplements, there are a few you should also consider taking.
         </p>
         <h2>
          Vitamin A
         </h2>
         <p>
          This is essential if you arent eating organ meats like beef liver, kidney, and heart (you should). Vitamin A is an important cofactor for numerous metabolic reactions and bodily functions. A quarter of Americans consume less than half the RDA, which is already too low. An important thing to remember is that you cant get vitamin A from plants. Plants dont have vitamin A, they have beta-carotene. Beta carotene is poorly converted into vitamin a which is why some populations develop vitamin A deficiency despite consuming far more than they should have required. Sorry vegetarians and vegans, carrots dont count.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Dose:
          </strong>
          10,000-15,000 IU / day.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Forms:
          </strong>
          Retinol (A good source of vitamin A is cod liver oil, which also has vitamin D)
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Time Taken:
          </strong>
          With meals.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Recommended Brand:
          </strong>
          Green Pasture Fermented Cod Liver Oil (Arctic Mint flavor)
         </p>
         <h2>
          Selenium
         </h2>
         <p>
          Selenium is a heavy metal with numerous beneficial effects on the body. It boosts immune function, prevents cancer, neurodegenerative disease, and protects against thyroid dysfunction. It is possible to get enough selenium from wild caught fish and animal products, but most people dont. If you cant find real meat, you should supplement with 200mcg per day. Be careful, too much selenium can cause negative health consequences. Take 200 micrograms, not milligrams.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Dose:
          </strong>
          200mcg / day
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Forms:
          </strong>
          Se Methyl Selenocysteine or selenomethionine
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Time Taken:
          </strong>
          Doesnt matter.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Recommended Brand:
          </strong>
          Life Extension
         </p>
         <h2>
          Copper
         </h2>
         <p>
          Copper is needed for proper vascular and heart function. Most of the U.S. Is woefully deficient in copper, consuming only .8mg per day. This is worrying since less than 1mg per day is enough to cause heart attacks. Copper intake has fallen over the last century due to modern farming and dietary practices. Modern fruits, vegetables, and conventional meats are low in copper, containing 75 percent less than they used to.
         </p>
         <p>
          Luckily, beef and lamb liver have a massive amount of copper. If youre eating at least four ounces of beef liver per week, you can meet your copper needs. Other good sources of copper include cocoa (dark chocolate  look for low toxin
          <a href="https://www.upgradedself.com/products/bulletproof-upgraded-chocolate-powder?utm_source=post&amp;utm_medium=blog&amp;utm_campaign=bulletproof-upgraded-coffee" target="_blank">
           Bulletproof Chocolate Powder
          </a>
          ), cashews, and lobster. If you arent eating beef or lamb liver weekly, you should supplement with at least 1mg per day.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Dose:
          </strong>
          1mg / day
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Forms:
          </strong>
          Capsule
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Time Taken:
          </strong>
          Doesnt matter.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Recommended Brand:
          </strong>
          Life Extension
         </p>
         <h2>
          B-12 and folinic acid
         </h2>
         <p>
          Most people are deficient in B12. B12 can protect against dementia, increase immune function, maintain nerves, and regenerate cells. B12 lowers homocysteine and protects against atherosclerosis. Its necessary for maintaining methylation reactions that repair DNA and prevent cancer. One of the most crucial areas for B12 is the brain.
         </p>
         <p>
          Folate deficiency can also cause mental symptoms, although B12 is more likely to be a problem. Folate and B12 are both required for mental function, and a deficiency in one produces a deficiency in the other, but folate will not correct a B12 deficiency in the brain. If you make the mistake of treating B12 deficiency with folate, you can get permanent brain damage. (hear that, vegans?) Likewise, high amounts of folate without adequate B12 can cause neurological conditions. Thats why I take them together.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Dose:
          </strong>
          &gt;5mg of methylcobalamin or hydroxycobalamin and &gt;800mcg of folate (5-MTHF or folinic acid, NOT folic acid)
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Forms:
          </strong>
          Capsule
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Time Taken:
          </strong>
          Doesnt matter.
         </p>
         <p>
          <strong>
           Recommended Brand:
          </strong>
          varies
         </p>
         <p>
          Supplementation is something everyone should do, but how much depends on your diet and other lifestyle factors. Athletes need more of some supplements than other people. In general, you should try to get as much nutrition from food as possible. You should consume nutrients in their most natural form. When you do supplement  you get what you pay for. If you arent wiling to spend money on quality supplements  youre compromising your health and it will cost more in the long term.
         </p>
         <h2>
          Looking for more?
         </h2>
         <p>
          The list above was a small portion of supplements to consider taking. This will provide you with a foundation for further supplementation with things like smart drugs and sleep hacking supplements. And dont forget the post about
          <a href="http://www.bulletproofexec.com/calcium-d-glucarate/">
           calcium-d-glucarate
          </a>
          !
         </p>
         <p>
          Learn about 11 more advanced biohacking supplements when you sign up for the Bulletproof Newsletter!
         </p>

          <li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" id="dsq-comment-4219">
           <div class="dsq-comment-header" id="dsq-comment-header-4219">
            <cite id="dsq-cite-4219">
             <span id="dsq-author-user-4219">
              Howard Lee Harkness
             </span>
            </cite>
           </div>
           <div class="dsq-comment-body" id="dsq-comment-body-4219">
            <div class="dsq-comment-message" id="dsq-comment-message-4219">
             <p>
              You left out B12. While you are at an age where B12 is probably not a problem, some of us have trouble absorbing enough, and the absorption problem generally starts getting worse in your mid-50s. Its cheap, and safe (no known LD50). There are no known side-effects from getting 1000x RDA or more. See my articles at
              <a href="http://nequals1health.com/could-it-be-b12/" rel="nofollow">
               http://nequals1health.com/could-it-be-b12/
              </a>
              and
              <a href="http://celtic-fiddler.com/fiddler/2011/07/could_it_be_b12/" rel="nofollow">
               http://celtic-fiddler.com/fiddler/2011/07/could_it_be_b12/
              </a>
              about the significant improvement I experienced in my hearing after starting high-dosage (2.5mg) sublingual B12.
             </p>
             <p>
              Also, B3 (niacin). 1500mg/day will significantly boost HDL. It will lower LDL better than any statin drug currently on the market, without making you feel like youve had the crap beaten out of you (at least in my case). It does have one harmless, but uncomfortable, side-effect: Flushing. It took me a year of gradual increase to get to 1500mg/day with only minor flushing.
             </p>
             <p>
              Copper: Ouch. I tried taking 1mg/day, and immediately started having severe leg cramps at night. I tried taking it every other day for a couple of weeks, and consistently got leg cramps only on the nights that I took the copper. Im not doing that any more.
             </p>
            </div>
           </div>

             <span id="dsq-author-user-4236">
              Jade
             </span>
            </cite>
           </div>
           <div class="dsq-comment-body" id="dsq-comment-body-4236">
            <div class="dsq-comment-message" id="dsq-comment-message-4236">
             <p>
              Dave  Please be very careful about implying that folic acid causes cancer! The study states that folic acid could be associated with additional risk for colon cancer. OK, however, it is widely known and accepted that woman taking folic acid supplementation at least 3mn prior to becoming pregnant reduce the risk for neural tube defects in their babies by 50-70%. Were fighting hard to get women in the habit of taking good  folic acid  prenatal vitamins in order to save babies. This needs to be said before we scare people away by claiming it causes cancer.
             </p>
            </div>
           </div>
           <ul class="children">
            <li class="comment even depth-2" id="dsq-comment-4237">
             <div class="dsq-comment-header" id="dsq-comment-header-4237">
              <cite id="dsq-cite-4237">
               <span id="dsq-author-user-4237">
                Dave Asprey
               </span>
              </cite>
             </div>
             <div class="dsq-comment-body" id="dsq-comment-body-4237">
              <div class="dsq-comment-message" id="dsq-comment-message-4237">
               <p>
                The problem is that many people arent capable of converting the synthetic form (folic acid) into the active form (folinic acid), so the synthetic form builds up. Thats bad news. So while some people can benefit from folic acid, many do not. However, everyone benefits equally from taking folinic acid (folate), so thats what we recommend for everyone.
                <br/>
                Put another way, if you have one supplement that always works, and one that sometimes works but is dangerous the rest of the time, which would you recommend? ?
               </p>
              </div>
             </div>
            </li>
           </ul>
          </li>

                <cite id="dsq-cite-5218">
                 <span id="dsq-author-user-5218">
                  Karen
                 </span>
                </cite>
               </div>
               <div class="dsq-comment-body" id="dsq-comment-body-5218">
                <div class="dsq-comment-message" id="dsq-comment-message-5218">
                 <p>
                  According to Dr. Mercola, a highly respected and knowlegeable physician IMO, I found in of his recent articles on the web, that he is of a different opinion regarding magnesium stearate. He states that it is a potentially hazardous ingredient. Magnesium stearate is essentially a chalk-like substance, which prevents the supplements from sticking together and allows the machinery to run smoother and faster, which equates to cost savings during the manufacturing process. Magnesium stearate is not a source of magnesium and has no benefits, but may have a detrimental effect on your immune function as stearic acid has been linked to suppression of T cells. The filler also stimulates your gut to form a biofilm, which can prevent proper absorption of nutrients in your digestive tract
                 </p>
                </div>
               </div>
               <ul class="children">
                <li class="comment even depth-4" id="dsq-comment-5382">
                 <div class="dsq-comment-header" id="dsq-comment-header-5382">
                  <cite id="dsq-cite-5382">
                   <span id="dsq-author-user-5382">
                    Dave Asprey
                   </span>
                  </cite>
                 </div>
                 <div class="dsq-comment-body" id="dsq-comment-body-5382">
                  <div class="dsq-comment-message" id="dsq-comment-message-5382">
                   <p>
                    Highly respected? Hardly.
                    <a href="http://www.bulletproofexec.com/its-official-dr-mercola-just-copied-the-bulletproof-diet/" rel="nofollow">
                     http://www.bulletproofexec.com/its-official-dr-mercola-just-copied-the-bulletproof-diet/
                    </a>
                    <br/>
                    Funny, the Mercola page includes an interview with Dr. Klinghardt, who is the source of the biofilm idea. I respect him a lot  in fact I shared a hotel room with him at an American Academy of Anti-aging Medicine conference once. Ive taken some courses from Dr. K. too. Now HE is credible
                    <br/>
                    Mercola says, I realize that there is very little research published on thisbut some highly respected clinicians like Dr. Klinghardt and others have extensive experience with this issue. Magnesium stearate is not a supplemental source of magnesium but it is a form of stearic acid and is used as a flow agent. The ONLY purpose of it in the supplement is to help the raw materials become more slippery and flow through the machines that create the supplements.
                    <br/>
                    I agree with Dr. Klinghardt about titanium dioxide (its not safe). But magnesium stearate is the magnesium form of stearic acid, which is a common fatty acid in meat. Without some sort of study about it, its hard to believe this is dangerous.
                    <br/>
                    To prevent the biofilm hypothesis, always take your vitamins with food so it will mix before hit hits the small intestine.
                   </p>
                  </div>
                 </div>

              <li class="comment odd alt depth-3" id="dsq-comment-4879">
               <div class="dsq-comment-header" id="dsq-comment-header-4879">
                <cite id="dsq-cite-4879">
                 <span id="dsq-author-user-4879">
                  Dave Asprey
                 </span>
                </cite>
               </div>
               <div class="dsq-comment-body" id="dsq-comment-body-4879">
                <div class="dsq-comment-message" id="dsq-comment-message-4879">
                 <p>
                  Too much vitamin c will cause you to get the runs. You can take it up to bowel tolerance. Individual needs vary greatly depending on how stressed you are or how sick you are. I can go from 3 g to 10 g very easily, but if I get a cold or something, I can often new 50+ grams a day without getting runs. The short answer is that your mileage may vary but you need enough vitamin c to make glutathione in your liver and collagen and the rest of your tissues. A couple grams does that for most people.
                 </p>
                </div>
               </div>

          <li class="comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="dsq-comment-4602">
           <div class="dsq-comment-header" id="dsq-comment-header-4602">
            <cite id="dsq-cite-4602">
             <span id="dsq-author-user-4602">
              TimR
             </span>
            </cite>
           </div>
           <div class="dsq-comment-body" id="dsq-comment-body-4602">
            <div class="dsq-comment-message" id="dsq-comment-message-4602">
             <p>
              Very useful, and this is not meant to be critical but I have to say Im extremely wary of supplements these days. Ive been trying to follow Paul Jaminets protocol (whose work is great by the way) but Ive run into so many side-effects and reactions its difficult.
             </p>
             <p>
              For instance I started getting this warm flushing feeling in my feet, which then became a hard-to-describe semi-tingling in my arms as well. I started cutting all my supplements to see if that was the cause. Finally I cut the K2 (from LE) that I was taking every four days. Did not seem likely based on supposed low risk of side effects, but my symptoms did stop and have not returned even as Ive added back some other supplements. There are so many variables maybe Im wrong, but Im wary of starting K2 again. Could it be that the high K2 aggravated an A deficiency? (Im not good about eating beef liver because it seems to coincide with bloating/ constipation/ digestive issues. Other A sources have their own issues, though Im trying to get at least weekly chicken livers.)
             </p>
             <p>
              You see what I mean though, it gets quite complicated!
             </p>
             <p>
              Not only do you have to understand the supplements themselves, you have to understand their co-factors and interactions with other minerals and nutrients, and your bodys current status, or risk drawing down something thats low by suddenly introducing a high dose of something.
             </p>
             <p>
              Another time I was having bizarre nightmares that would cause me to wake feeling anxious and very uneasy and sleep fitfully after that. I definitely pegged it to liquid Vit D3 supplements, because it would reliably happen that night after taking D3 in the morning, and not happen if I skipped the D3. Also it happened with multiple brands of liquid D3. Still dont know what this response really means, I just know Im only getting D from sunlight for now..!
             </p>
            </div>
           </div>

           <ul class="children">
            <li class="comment even depth-2" id="dsq-comment-20018">
             <div class="dsq-comment-header" id="dsq-comment-header-20018">
              <cite id="dsq-cite-20018">
               <span id="dsq-author-user-20018">
                Alex James
               </span>
              </cite>
             </div>
             <div class="dsq-comment-body" id="dsq-comment-body-20018">
              <div class="dsq-comment-message" id="dsq-comment-message-20018">
               <p>
                You might be referring to this article: Taking Oral Vitamin D? Avoid Making This Serious Mistake
                <a href="http://articles.mercola.com/sites/articles/archive/2012/02/23/oral-vitamin-d-mistake.aspx" rel="nofollow">
                 http://articles.mercola.com/sites/articles/archive/2012/02/23/oral-vitamin-d-mistake.aspx
                </a>
               </p>
               <p>
                Dr Mercola doesnt recommend against taking vitamin D. He does say that sunlight or safe tanning bed exposure are preferable to oral supplementation, because it promotes natural synthesis of cholecalciferol AND other compounds he believes beneficial (cholesterol sulphate, cholecalciferol sulphate). But, in his own words if neither of these are feasible options, then you should take an oral
                <br/>
                vitamin D3 supplement. It will certainly be better than no vitamin D at
                <br/>
                all.
               </p>
               <p>
                This comes with the caveat that you are supplementing D3 (cholecalciferol) specifically, and not artificial D2 (ergocalciferol), which has been shown to marginally increase mortality. (
                <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22552031" rel="nofollow">
                 http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/22552031
                </a>
                )
               </p>
              </div>
             </div>
            </li>
           </ul>

                 <p>
                  THIS ! If you have autoimmune thyroiditis under NO circumstances should you take iodine supplementation  it can cause a thyroid storm. Its one of the most common forms of hypothyroidism and its really, really important to establish if you have it (via Thyroid antibody testing) before supplementing with iodine. Iodine deficiency is rarer than youd think as cooking salt is iodised. (And bread flour here in Australia, not that we eats grains
                  <img alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" src="//www.bulletproofexec.com/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;"/>
                  I would honestly suggest eating more small, oily fish and using iodised cooking salt if you want to increase your iodine intake. I seriously wouldnt supplement  apart from anything else, too much kelp can actually cause hypothyroidism.
                 </p>

              Comes to $106 if ordered from iHerb + $10 shipping to Australia. I didnt count the D3 as I already have a huge jar of them  I get the Healthy Origins Brand at $16.95 for 360 at 5,000iu per capsule. I also wanted some NAC and went with the Jarrow non-slow release.
             </p>
             <p>
              Speaking as someone with Hashimotos, who has to take huge amounts of supplements due to a malfunctioning autoimmune system, I actually dont think this is too bad in terms of a supplementation regime. Ive walked out of a Doctors with $300 worth of supplements before  and often for a 2 month supply. The above order will last me 3 months at least, and some, like the D3 are a years supply.
             </p>
             <p>
              I also take the Solar sublingual b12, the Now Milk thistle (I do a course once or twice a year) and the Now borage oil. I find Optimoz do the best prices for the MCT Oil, coffee etc
              <a href="http://www.optimoz.com.au/" rel="nofollow">
               http://www.optimoz.com.au/
              </a>
             </p>
             <p>
              Its all good, but I have to say that most of my friends think Im nuts. I was showing my girlfriends my pill case yesterday and I got some raised eyebrows. I think that unless youve had a chronic illness which doesnt respond well to medication, you cant really understand what a difference it makes to find a supplement which allows you to function better.
             </p>
             <p>
              I dont got to all this trouble and expense so that I can hone a finely developed physique and mental performance.. I do this so that I can function without falling asleep at 1pm in the afternoon, or hitting 300 pounds.
             </p>
             <p>
              I find it very useful to have Bodyhackers do the footwork for me. Hell, maybe one of these days I may even lose some weight 
             </p>
             <p>
              Thanks Dave!

              Rick

           </div>
           <div class="dsq-comment-body" id="dsq-comment-body-15910">
            <div class="dsq-comment-message" id="dsq-comment-message-15910">
             <p>
              Great article, just one small nit to pick. Calling ascorbic acid Vitamin C is like going to a tire store, pointing to 4 tires and saying you have a car. Theyre assuredly part of a car, but if thats all youve got, youre not going anywhere. When the body receives ascorbic acid its also expecting to receive a number of other phyto-compounds that allow the body to properly utilize it. Taking ascorbic acid by itself is essentially taking a drug, not a nutrient. Not saying thats a bad thing, but if you want Vitamin C, Id suggest a food-based product like the excellent one from The Synergy Company, Pure Radiance C. I dont work for them, Ive just used the product for a few years and found it to be very beneficial. Ill occasionally use straight ascorbic acid when dealing with certain issues, but I use the above product as my daily vitamin C supplement.
             </p>
            </div>
           </div>
          </li>

Initially, I felt a more energetic and on the ball, but within a week I was experiencing brain fog, mild dizziness, and visual distortions. On stopping, things returned to normal, but what a surprising effect!

I want to upgrade myself as much as possible, but this seems like it could be downgrading your body. Just doesnt seem like it would help your body or be beneficial. Where is the proof? I know multis have shown to lead to shorter lifespans. Sounds like the pharma companies are just trying to make another buck off this conspiracy. Your insight would be greatly appreciated Dave/guys
             </p>
            </div>
           </div>

             <p>
              You should really mention that magnesium citrate =/= magnesium.
              <br/>
              1,9 grams of magnesium citrate equal about 315 mg of magnesium.
             </p>
             <p>
              I was a little concerned at first about the high dosage of my supplement since you only recommend up to 800 mg, but then I realized I need to take 4-5 grams of magnesium citrate to reach 700-800mg magnesium from it.
             </p>
             <p>
              So definitely room for confusion there.
             </p>

           <div class="dsq-comment-header" id="dsq-comment-header-25982">
            <cite id="dsq-cite-25982">
             <span id="dsq-author-user-25982">

             </span>

           <div class="dsq-comment-body" id="dsq-comment-body-25982">
            <div class="dsq-comment-message" id="dsq-comment-message-25982">

              Hi, what does the IU in 10,000-15,000 IU / day stand for?? Am I just being simple?
             </p>

           <ul class="children">
            <li class="comment even depth-2" id="dsq-comment-26794">
             <div class="dsq-comment-header" id="dsq-comment-header-26794">
              <cite id="dsq-cite-26794">
               <span id="dsq-author-user-26794">
                Hendo
               </span>
              </cite>
             </div>
             <div class="dsq-comment-body" id="dsq-comment-body-26794">
              <div class="dsq-comment-message" id="dsq-comment-message-26794">
               <p>
                Hello MM, IU stands for International Unit
               </p>
               <p>
                The volume or mass that makes up one International unit is dependent on the concentration or potency of the substance and therefore varies from substance to substance depending on what is being measured.
               </p>
               <p>
                Further reading here:

              Nicolas Echeverria
             </span>
            </cite>
           </div>
           <div class="dsq-comment-body" id="dsq-comment-body-31000">
            <div class="dsq-comment-message" id="dsq-comment-message-31000">
             <p>
              Green Pastures does not list the Retinol dosage on their Fermented Cod Liver Oil. How much is everyone else taking? The recommended does is 2mL. Is it possible that I am getting too much Retinol with this dosage?
             </p>
             <p>
              Also, can anyone recommend another brand of Bulletproof Retinol supplement? Preferably one that is less expensive, in capsule form, and has a minimal amount of anti-nutrients (mercury, GMOs, etc.)
             </p>
             <p>
              Sidenote: Do not buy Green Pastures Cod Liver Oil from Amazon. Get it directly from the manufacturer. 20% mark-ups on Amazon.
             </p>
